## Section 001: Tdd Progress Journal Schema
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names a journal schema without saying what problem the schema solves, keeping a TDD session resumable after context loss by recording phase, test status, and next steps in a fixed shape
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because long-running agent sessions lose context between checkpoints, and only a fixed-shape entry lets a successor reconstruct where the red-green-refactor loop stood
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a checkpoint schema adds pure overhead on one-sitting tasks that finish before any context loss can occur
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the schema governs checkpoint entries for TDD-style work and does not prescribe the tests, the code design, or the commit discipline around them
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open by stating that this schema exists so a fresh session can resume mid-loop from the journal alone, without rereading the whole transcript
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a journal entry is written for a reader who shares none of the writer's working memory, which is why every field must be self-contained
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to write one schema-shaped checkpoint entry per work batch, always naming the phase, exact test names with statuses, and a numbered next step
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because long-running agent sessions lose context between checkpoints, and only a fixed-shape entry lets a successor reconstruct where the red-green-refactor loop stood
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a checkpoint schema adds pure overhead on one-sitting tasks that finish before any context loss can occur
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the schema governs checkpoint entries for TDD-style work and does not prescribe the tests, the code design, or the commit discipline around them
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open by stating that this schema exists so a fresh session can resume mid-loop from the journal alone, without rereading the whole transcript
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a journal entry is written for a reader who shares none of the writer's working memory, which is why every field must be self-contained
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the work follows a red-green-refactor rhythm, sessions can be interrupted, and a durable journal file persists between them
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because long-running agent sessions lose context between checkpoints, and only a fixed-shape entry lets a successor reconstruct where the red-green-refactor loop stood
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where a checkpoint schema adds pure overhead on one-sitting tasks that finish before any context loss can occur
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by the schema governs checkpoint entries for TDD-style work and does not prescribe the tests, the code design, or the commit discipline around them
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the work follows a red-green-refactor rhythm, sessions can be interrupted, and a durable journal file persists between them
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that a journal entry is written for a reader who shares none of the writer's working memory, which is why every field must be self-contained
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: a checkpoint schema adds pure overhead on one-sitting tasks that finish before any context loss can occur
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are entries degrade into vague prose once a session feels fluent, and the phase field silently goes stale when work pivots mid-batch
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the work follows a red-green-refactor rhythm, sessions can be interrupted, and a durable journal file persists between them
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using the schema governs checkpoint entries for TDD-style work and does not prescribe the tests, the code design, or the commit discipline around them
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: commit messages as a coarse journal for small tasks, issue-tracker comments for team-visible work, or a full transcript dump when storage is cheap and review is not needed
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the minimum task size where journaling pays for itself is unmeasured, so the overhead threshold stays judgment
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: commit messages as a coarse journal for small tasks, issue-tracker comments for team-visible work, or a full transcript dump when storage is cheap and review is not needed

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: alternatives become option theater when entries degrade into vague prose once a session feels fluent, and the phase field silently goes stale when work pivots mid-batch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare only choices allowed by the schema governs checkpoint entries for TDD-style work and does not prescribe the tests, the code design, or the commit discipline around them
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: revise the guidance to contrast the default with each viable recovery and apply this section-specific change: open by stating that this schema exists so a fresh session can resume mid-loop from the journal alone, without rereading the whole transcript
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tdd Progress Journal Schema", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: make the tradeoff consequential by connecting it to a journal entry is written for a reader who shares none of the writer's working memory, which is why every field must be self-contained

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the mapping cannot show which copy is maintained going forward, so citing either path risks pointing at the one that later rots
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table records provenance for this document's claims and does not decide which mirrored copy the archive should keep
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to annotate the two local rows as one schema mirrored across the 202602 orchestrator and 202604 retainer skill folders, and mark external rows retrieval-undated

## Section 003: Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scoreboard awards 95, 91, and 88 to generic corpus hygiene and never ranks the journaling practices the schema teaches, phase honesty, exact test naming, and next-step continuity
- **supporting_reason:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because attention follows the ranking, and a scoreboard silent about phase and test fields lets writers polish citations while entries stop being resumable
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the numbers have no measurement behind them in this corpus, so quoting them as evidence rather than editorial emphasis misleads

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists three corpus-hygiene failures and omits the journaling failures the schema's own rules imply, phaseless entries, vague test references, missing next steps, and diary-style prose
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a reviewer triaging a stalled resume needs named journal failures with detection signals, not generic advice hygiene
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rows that cannot be matched against an actual journal entry detect nothing at the moment of resumption
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry covers entry-writing failures, not TDD malpractice like skipping the red step, which the source skill's workflow owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add phaseless-entry, unnamed-test-reference, missing-next-step, and prose-drift rows, each detectable by scanning an entry against the schema fields
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that every journal anti-pattern is a resume failure waiting for the worst moment, and all four are mechanically detectable
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a reviewer triaging a stalled resume needs named journal failures with detection signals, not generic advice hygiene
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; rows that cannot be matched against an actual journal entry detect nothing at the moment of resumption
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the registry covers entry-writing failures, not TDD malpractice like skipping the red step, which the source skill's workflow owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add phaseless-entry, unnamed-test-reference, missing-next-step, and prose-drift rows, each detectable by scanning an entry against the schema fields
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies every journal anti-pattern is a resume failure waiting for the worst moment, and all four are mechanically detectable

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names the repository verifier for this document and gives no check for journal entries themselves, whose completeness is scannable field by field
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because entry completeness is the cheapest gate in this theme because the schema enumerates required fields that a scan can confirm without judgment
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: no scan can judge whether a next step is genuinely actionable, so mechanical gates need a paired human read for quality
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: gates here verify this reference and journal-entry form, not the test suites the journal reports on, which have their own commands
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add an entry-completeness check, phase present, at least one test with status, numbered next step, run before any checkpoint is declared done
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that gating the journal at write time is vastly cheaper than discovering the gap at resume time, when the writer's context is gone

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide gives the four stock bullets and never says when journaling applies, any multi-batch or interruptible task, or when it is overhead, single-sitting work finished before context can decay
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the schema pays exactly when future context loss is plausible, so admission turns on task duration and interruption risk, not on topic keywords
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: journaling every trivial errand teaches agents the schema is ceremony, which corrodes compliance on the long tasks that need it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide admits tasks into journal-keeping and does not rank this reference against neighbors, which the routing section owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to key admission to task shape, journal when work spans batches, sessions, or owners, and skip with a note when a task completes in one warm sitting
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the decision to journal must be made at task start, because by the time context loss proves the need, the unjournaled context is already gone
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scenario opens with a lead turning ambiguity into acceptance criteria and stops before any journaling happens, no entry written, no interruption survived, no resume demonstrated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the schema's value is only visible across an interruption, so a journey that never loses context cannot show why the fields matter
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a journey without a resume event argues the journal is bookkeeping, the exact belief that kills compliance
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the scenario illustrates one representative interruption-and-resume arc, not a claim that every task hits context loss
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the journey through a written Green-phase entry, a session end, and a successor session resuming from the entry alone

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table keys adopt, adapt, and avoid to generic evidence agreement instead of the variables that govern journaling cost, task length, interruption risk, and how many hands the work passes through
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because full-schema entries pay on long multi-owner work, trimmed entries suit short solo work, and the wrong calibration either burns time or strands a successor
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: avoid chosen for a long task is discovered only at resume time, when the absent journal cannot be written retroactively
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide calibrates journaling depth for this theme and cannot excuse skipping the completion rules once an entry is being written at all
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rekey adopt to multi-session or multi-owner work, adapt to compressed entries on short solo work, and avoid to one-sitting tasks with an explicit skip note
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that journaling depth is insurance pricing, and the premium should track the cost of losing the context, not the writer's enthusiasm

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds work at twenty requirement IDs and one traceability matrix, spec-theme units, and its source-pressure cell truncates mid-list, while journaling workload is really bounded by batch size between checkpoints
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the risk this schema manages is context accumulating unjournaled, so the natural workload unit is the batch a single entry must cover
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a session honoring requirement-ID caps can still run six hours without a checkpoint, losing everything the model was meant to protect
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds journaling cadence and entry scope, not the engineering workload the journal reports on
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rederive the boundary as one entry per coherent batch, checkpoint before any risky operation, and never more than a session between entries, repairing the truncated cell

- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because triage at a broken resume needs rows describing how journals fail, ranked by silence, and every journal failure is silent until resumption
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rows are worthless if their earliest signal fires only after the resume has already stalled

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify verification failures and cap retries but never define journal-specific semantics, what to do when an entry cannot be written honestly or a resume finds the journal insufficient
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because an unwritable entry means the work state is not understood, and pressing on multiplies the very confusion the journal exists to contain
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: retrying the resume against the same insufficient journal reproduces the stall, since the missing context is not in the file
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs journal-write and resume retries, not retries of the tests and builds the journal reports
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add journal semantics, halt work when an honest entry cannot be written, and on an insufficient resume reconstruct once from artifacts then escalate with the gap named
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that inability to write a checkpoint is itself the highest-value signal, because it means the current state would already fail a resume
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to stop at any batch boundary where phase or test status cannot be stated, resolve the ambiguity, write the entry, then resume work
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because an unwritable entry means the work state is not understood, and pressing on multiplies the very confusion the journal exists to contain
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; retrying the resume against the same insufficient journal reproduces the stall, since the missing context is not in the file
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this governs journal-write and resume retries, not retries of the tests and builds the journal reports
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add journal semantics, halt work when an honest entry cannot be written, and on an insufficient resume reconstruct once from artifacts then escalate with the gap named

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets recycle source-loading and latency records and never treat the journal itself as the observability instrument whose own health needs watching
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because in this theme the journal is the telemetry, so observability means keeping the instrument honest, entries timely, fields complete, and claims consistent with artifacts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: meta-records about the journal can outgrow the journal, doubling the writing burden that already competes with work
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this covers observing journal health, while the journal itself observes the work, two layers that must not be conflated
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recenter the checklist on instrument health, entry timestamps against work activity, completion-rule scan results, and spot-checks of entry claims against diffs and test output
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a journal is trustworthy exactly to the degree its claims are spot-checkable against artifacts that did not pass through the writer
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record scan results beside each entry, keep timestamps honest, and cross-check one claim per review against the repository state
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because in this theme the journal is the telemetry, so observability means keeping the instrument honest, entries timely, fields complete, and claims consistent with artifacts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; meta-records about the journal can outgrow the journal, doubling the writing burden that already competes with work
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this covers observing journal health, while the journal itself observes the work, two layers that must not be conflated
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: recenter the checklist on instrument health, entry timestamps against work activity, completion-rule scan results, and spot-checks of entry claims against diffs and test output

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method demands full REQ-to-test mapping and latency packets, spec-theme machinery, while this schema's performance is resume speed and checkpoint overhead, neither of which is mentioned
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the schema performs well when resumes are fast and checkpoint writing stays cheap, so verification must time those two paths, not requirement traceability
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the two measures trade off, since richer entries speed resumes but cost more to write, and measuring only one hides the trade
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this evaluates the schema's operational cost and benefit, not the performance of the software under development
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure minutes from session start to first productive action on resumes, and entry-writing time per checkpoint, comparing against unjournaled task baselines
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the schema's return on investment is concentrated in its worst case, the resume that would otherwise require full transcript archaeology

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement recites multi-system and SLO limits and misses the journal-specific scale walls, entries ballooning past skimmability, many agents sharing one journal, and journals outliving their tasks unarchived
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because journals fail at scale through interleaving and bloat, since a resume must skim history linearly and concurrent writers shred the phase field's meaning
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a shared phase field is undefined when three lanes write concurrently, which is a structural limit no writing discipline fixes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the boundaries bound the journal discipline, not the size of the engineering effort being journaled
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add journal-scale signals, per-lane journals once writers multiply, summarize-and-archive once history exceeds a skimmable length, and close journals when tasks end
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that this corpus already sharded, master journal for Red-Green-Refactor transitions and lane journals for batch detail, which is the pattern the boundary prescribes
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to one journal per lane per task, a summary entry every dozen or so entries, and archive on task completion
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because journals fail at scale through interleaving and bloat, since a resume must skim history linearly and concurrent writers shred the phase field's meaning
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a shared phase field is undefined when three lanes write concurrently, which is a structural limit no writing discipline fixes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the boundaries bound the journal discipline, not the size of the engineering effort being journaled
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add journal-scale signals, per-lane journals once writers multiply, summarize-and-archive once history exceeds a skimmable length, and close journals when tasks end
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies this corpus already sharded, master journal for Red-Green-Refactor transitions and lane journals for batch detail, which is the pattern the boundary prescribes
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the boundaries assume identifiable lanes, a place to archive, and resumes that read recent entries rather than whole histories
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because journals fail at scale through interleaving and bloat, since a resume must skim history linearly and concurrent writers shred the phase field's meaning
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where a shared phase field is undefined when three lanes write concurrently, which is a structural limit no writing discipline fixes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by the boundaries bound the journal discipline, not the size of the engineering effort being journaled
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the boundaries assume identifiable lanes, a place to archive, and resumes that read recent entries rather than whole histories
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that this corpus already sharded, master journal for Red-Green-Refactor transitions and lane journals for batch detail, which is the pattern the boundary prescribes
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
